2016-04-04 23:42:10	ScruffyChat	And it'll soften the whole image, eliminating some fireflies at the cost of other tiny details that may have been present

2016-04-10 18:22:34	ScruffyChat	Oh, Espyo, I think I have an explanation for the bomb rocks' energy looking bloated when viewed from afar through the camera
2016-04-10 18:23:01	ScruffyChat	It has to do with the camera's depth of field function, which turns distant objects blurry if close objects are in autofocus
2016-04-10 18:23:23	ScruffyChat	Normally bomb rocks are spheres that are easy to blur and calculate distance
2016-04-10 18:23:27	<--	Neocraftz1553 (Mibbit@206.78.wr.nm) has quit (Quit: http://www.mibbit.com ajax IRC Client)
2016-04-10 18:23:29	ScruffyChat	But emitted light is not
2016-04-10 18:23:45	ScruffyChat	Especially when it's as powerful emitted light as the bomb rocks have
2016-04-10 18:23:58	ScruffyChat	So I think it miscalculates their blur
2016-04-10 18:31:38	@Espyo	ah, might make sense, yes

2016-04-14 19:51:30	Yoshi2	to my editor I added moving the level view by dragging the mouse across the view earlier today, I'm suprised it was so easy
2016-04-14 19:51:43	ScruffyChat	Nice!
2016-04-14 19:52:28	@Espyo	yeah, that's usually how it is
2016-04-14 19:52:30	@Espyo	you do it
2016-04-14 19:52:31	@Espyo	and
2016-04-14 19:52:36	@Espyo	sometimes... that's all there is to it
2016-04-14 19:52:36	Yoshi2	the basic idea is: 1) if user clicks the mouse, set dragging = True and set lastx = current x, lasty = current y 2) if user releases the mouse, set dragging = False
2016-04-14 19:52:39	@Espyo	specially on stuff like this
2016-04-14 19:52:43	@Espyo	yep
2016-04-14 19:53:21	Yoshi2	3) while moving the mouse, calculate current x - lastx and current y - lasty and move the screen by -deltax and -deltay
2016-04-14 19:54:01	Yoshi2	(because you want to move the screen in the opposite direction of the dragging, not in the direction of dragging)
2016-04-14 19:54:06	@Espyo	yeah
